This shows that almost all stanzas quoted by the *Śrīmūlam* commentator in the first and second parts of the commentary are either from Bhaṭṭasvāmī or from the anonymous Malayalam commentator. Further, Ganapati Sastri owes much to the Malayalam commentary for giving details which are otherwise unknown. The following is an instance. In the II Adhikaraṇa called Adhyakṣaprakāra, Kauṭalya gives the source of pearls as follows :

 ताम्रपर्णिकं, पाण्ड्यकवाटं, पाशिक्यं, कौलेयं, चौर्णेयं, माहेन्द्रं, कार्दमिकं स्त्रौतसीयं, ह्रादीयं, हैमवतं च मौक्तिकम् ।

The *Śrīmūlam* commentator is able to give a detailed account as follows :⁴⁷

^(\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_)

^(47.) *TSS* 79, p. 179

 ताम्रपर्णिकं, ताम्रपर्णी नाम पाण्ड्येषु प्रसिद्धा नदी तस्याः समुद्रसङ्गमप्रदेशे समुत्पन्नं, पाण्ड्यकवाटं मलयकोटिपर्वतोत्पन्नं, पाशिक्यं पाटलिपुत्रान्तिकगतायां पाशिकाख्यायां नद्यामुत्पन्नं, कौलेयं सिंहलद्वीपे मयूरग्रामे कुसानाम नदी तस्यामुत्पन्नं, चौर्णेयं केरलेषु मुरचिनामकपतनसमीपे चूर्णी नाम नदी तस्यामुत्पन्नं, माहेन्द्रं महेन्द्रपर्वताम्यर्णाम्भोधिसंभवं, कार्दमिकं कर्दमा नाम पारसीकेषु नदी तस्यामुत्पन्नं, स्रौतसीयं बर्बरकुले स्रोतसी नाम नदी तस्यामुत्पन्नं, ह्लदीयं बर्बरकूले समुद्रेकदेशे श्रीघण्टो नाम ह्रदः तस्मिन्नुत्पन्नं, हैमवतं च हिमालयसम्भवं भवति । इत्थं मौक्तिकस्योत्पत्तिक्षेत्राणि दश भवन्ति।

This is only a translation of the following original in Malayalam given by the ancient Malayalam commentator of Kerala.⁴⁸

 “Tāmraparṇpikamāvo tāmraparṇiporuttil janikkintavu. Pāṇḍyakavāṭamāvitu malayako- ṭiyākinṭa parvatattil uḷuvākinṭavu. Pāśikyamāvo pāśikyamymāvo pāṭaliputranarike ullitoru āttil ulavāmavu. Kauleyamāvitu īlanāttil mayūragrāmattil kūla ākinṭa āttil ulavāmavu. Caurṇeyamāvitu malanāṭṭil muraci akinṭa paṭṭinttinnarike cūrniyāttil ulavāmavu. Mahendrakamavitu Māhendraparvatattinna rike kataṭlilulavāmavu. Kārdamikamāvinṭavu conināttil kardama ākinṭa nadiyil ulavāmavu. Srotasīyamāvitu papparakūlattil oriṭattu Śrīghaṇṭam enpitu samudrattil srotasi ākinṭa āttil janikkumavu. Hrādīyamāvitu papparakūlattil oru kayam atil ulavākinṭavu. Haimavatamāvitu himavān melullitorāttil ulavāmavu. Ava pattu ksotrañnalāvo”.

 Shama Sastri who did not have the benefit of consulting the Malayalam commentary translates Māhendra and Haimavata as obtaining from the respective mountain regions whereas Ganapati Sastri following the ancient Malayalam commer establishes that these varieties are obtained from the rivers flowing near the respective mountain regions. Thus Shama Sastri’s translation of the above passage remains vague.⁴⁹

 Further, the Malayalam commentary has helped Ganapati Sastri to explain many of the stories alluded to in the Sūtras of *Kauṭalīya.* For instance, towards the end of the Samayācārika

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

^(48.) Kautaliya with Malayalam commentary, Pt II, pp. 93-94

^(49.) Eng. trans. p. 77

in the fifth Adhikaraṇa called Yogavṛtta many such stories are hinted at. All of them are explained in detail by the Malayālam commentator though he does not reveal the source of his information. Ganapati Sastri has either translated or adapted such stories in his commentary on such occasions. An instance may be noted here. In explaining the passage : रथाश्वं प्राशंसीदिति पिशुनःthe *Śrīmulam* commentary states :⁵⁰

 इयमिह कथा – पिशुनो नामाचार्य उज्जयिन्यां प्रद्योतस्य पुत्रं पालकं नोतिविद्यामध्यापयाम्बभूव । अथ समाप्तेऽध्यापने राजा पिशुनस्य धनमपहर्तुममन्त्रयत स्वपुत्रसन्निधौ । तच्छ्रुत्वा पुत्र प्राचार्यद्रोहं परिजिहीर्षुः स्यन्दनमश्वयुक्तमारुह्याचार्यस्याग्रे स्थित्वा रथाश्वं श्लाघितवान्— अश्वोऽयमेकाह्ना त्रिशतं योजनानि गच्छेदिति । तेनात्मगमनं चोदितं ज्ञात्वा पिशुनस्ततोगतइति।

 This story is an epitomised version of the Malayalam commentary which is as follows:⁵¹

“Terkkutira varaṇiccatu kaṇṭu poyān piśunan. Piśunan ākinṭa ācāryan ujjayiniyinkal Pradyotanuṭaya makan Pālakanai nityam nūru pon koṇṭu nitiśāstram oticcān. Anantaram nītiśāstram poyappinnai ivanuṭaya pon pariccu kolvitentu Pālakan keḷkka mantriccān. Atu keṭṭu, brāhmaṇaṇākayumoṇṭu, ācāryanākeyumoṇṭu, ivanai drohiyāte viṭaveṇṭumentu ninaiccu termeleri, ācāryan munnal miṇṭu, terkkutirakalai varṇiccān. “Oru nāḷile pūrukātam cellum”, entān. Atu keṭṭu avanum ennuṭaya gamanam ivan collītentu ninaccu poyān”.

In the oriental version it is said that Pālaka was taught at a daily fee of one hundred gold pieces. The boy decided to save his teacher with the added reason that he happened to be a Brahmin. These aspects are omitted by Ganapati Sastri in his adaptation. Similarly, the stories of Kaṇiṅka, Ghoṭamukha, Kiñjalka and Piśunaputra are also explained by the *Śrīmūlam* commentator following the original lines of the Malayalam commentator without acknowledging the fact. No other commentator has given such details on these passages.

 Similarly, in the explanation of certain kārikas, the

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

^(50.) *TSS* 80, p. 216

^(51.) *Bhāṣākauṭalīyam,* p. 227

*Śrīmulam* commentary has derived inspiration from the Malayalam original, though the fact is seldom acknowledged. An instance may be noted here :

**दृष्टदोषःस्वयंवादः स्वपक्षपरपक्षयोः ।  
अनुयोगार्जवं हेतुः शपथश्चार्थसाधकः॥**

This pithy stanza is explained in detail by Ganapati Sastri as follows :⁵²Dṛṣṭadoṣaḥ: the one exhibiting evidence of his guilt, for instance a man standing in a house on fire holding a torch suggests that he has set the house ablaze. Similarly, in a scene of fight the one holding the sword soaked in blood suggests that he has wounded others from whom fresh blood is oozing. *Svayaṁvadaḥ :* one who proclaims that he had done the act under dispute. The word *Arthasādhaka* is explained as the truthful statement of the witness to the advocate. For instance, on the way the driver of a cart broke the foot of a man by driving the wheel over it. The injured took him to an officer who asked the driver as to why he did it. The driver being afraid could not speak even a word and the officer began to think that the fellow must be dumb. Then the bystanders reported to the officer that they have heard his exhortations to give way by asking them to move from the course of the cart. In this instance, the reports of the witnesses are prompted by truth and as such helpful to decide the issue. *Hetu* or sufficient reason is explained as the assertion of one that he is a eunuch when confronted with the accusation of being an adulterer. *Śapatha* is explained as a *divyakriyā* divine act to prove innocence.

 The above explanation is almost a word by word translation of the Malayalam commentary. The only difference consis in the medium of language. The original passage is as follows :⁵³

 “Dṛṣṭadoṣanāvon kāṇappeṭṭa doṣattai uṭayavan. Avanudoṣam orarthasādhakan entavāru. Vekinta illattinakattu tikkoḷḷi piṭicou ninton ivan cuṭṭonentu koḷvitu. Vaḷakkāṭiyeṭattu oruttanmel puṇṇuṇṭāyirippatu, mattavanāyudhattinmel

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

⁵²*TSS.* 80, p. 11

⁵³*Kauṭalīyam* Malayalam commentary Pt. III, pp. 13-14

rudhiram uṇṭāyirikkil avanai ivane veṭṭiyon entu arivitu entijjāti. Svayamādamāvitu ñān itu ceyten entu collumatu. Svapakṣaparapkṣayoranuyoranuyogārjavamentavāru abhiyoktavu ṛjuvāyñṭu abhiyojyanukku doṣamillāma tontumāru abhiyogippatu. Atinnudāharaṇam— Śākaṭikan cāṭṭinuruḷkkonṭṭu vaḷiyil veccu enkāl muriccānentu anyāyappeṭṭappoṇentinnivanuṭeya kāl muriccutentu vicāriccāl bhayappaṭṭu śākaṭikan miṇṭāte irinnatukaṇṭu ivanorumūkano entu vicāriccappoṇ abhiyoktāvu colluvitu. Cāṭṭinmeleriyiruntellārum keḷkka akalanillentu palmureyum collintappoṇ mukanāyitilla. Ippoṇ mūkanāyirunnonentu avanu doṣamillāttavāru ārjavattināl collumatu entivaṇṇam kaṇṭukoḷka. Hetuvāvitu kāraṇam kāṭṭi collintatu. Ivan pāradāradārikan entu abhiyogiccappoṇñān napumsakan entumariyiccal pāradārikanallāma sāddhikkum. Añcāmatu śapatham. Atuvum arthasādhakam. Atuvum tulārohaṇādi”.

 The last portion *tulārohaṇa* is translated by Ganapati Sastri as *divyakriyā*since very often accused persons are weighed in a scale before temples to prove their guilt or innocence as the case may be.

 In explaining the technical term also the Malayalam commentary has become the basis of *Śrīmūlam* on many occasions. For instance, *Rājavarṣa* is explained as regnal year of the king.⁵⁴ The Malayalam commentary gives an illustration mentioning the name of king Mahāsena. It states that the records must be written “in the particular year of king Mahāsena etc”. Ganapati Sastri has omitted the name and has generally given the substance as in “in the regnal year of so and so etc.”Similarly, the word ‘Mūrvā’is explained in the *Śrimūlam* commentary as :⁵⁵

मूर्वामरुतिति द्रविडदेशप्रसिद्धा

based on the Malayalam passage: “Mūrvāyāvitu maralentu draviḷadeśattil prasiddham”.

 In dealing with yantras the variety called *Bahumukha* is described as three or four-storeyed structure on wheels so

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

⁵⁴TSS 79, p. 138; Mal. Com. II, p. 44

⁵⁵Ibid. p. 247; Ibid, p. 187

that the archers could climb over it and send the arrows intothe fortification.⁵⁶ The idea is borrowed from the Malayalamcommentary, The passages may be quoted here: बहुमुखं प्रकारोत्सेवातिगतश्चक्रसन्निविष्टश्चर्यावृतस्त्रिचतुस्तलोधामुष्काधिष्ठानं च अट्टालकोभवति, तत्र स्थिता धन्विनो नराः सर्वतः शरान्क्षिपन्ति ।

The relevant Malayalam passage contains the entire idea :“Bahumukhamāvitu prākārattil cāṭṭil uyaramuṇṭāy uruḷumuṇṭāymūntu tān nālu tān nīlayumuṇṭāy tolkoṇṭu ceyvitoru aṭṭāl.Atinmel nintu purattuninta villālikaḷkku durgattinakattiṭṭueyyalāvitentu.”

In the same way other machines like *Sarvatobhadra*, *Jāmadagnya* etc are closely described following the details suppliedby the Malayalam commentator. As a result even the specifications could be supplied in the Sanskrit commentary by itsauthor.

 This kind of dependence for details and real significancecan be noticed in the *Śrīmūlam* commentary upto the end of the7th Adhikaraṇa for which portion the Malayalam commentaryis available at present.

*Influence of Nayacandrikā*: Yet another commentary thatbecame useful to Ganapati Sastri was *Nayacandrikā* of Mādhavayajvan. With its help he could compose his gloss upto the penultimate Adhyāya of the 12th Adhikaraṇa. Though he hasextensively used the commentary, he has expressly mentionedthe work only on 11 occasions. On four occasions he quotespassages and mentions the *Nayacandrikā* commentary. Thename of the author Mādhava is stated on seven instances inthe course of the four Adhikaraṇasfrom eight to twelve. Allthe references occur in the third part of the *Śrīmūlam* commentary comprising Adhikaraṇas eight to fifteen of the *Arthaśāstra*.The following are the references:

 **(1)** AdhikaraṇaVIII, p. 24

 ‘अन्येषां’इति पाठो मूलमातृकासु न दृश्यते। किन्तु नयचन्द्रिकाया-

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

⁵⁶TSS 79, p. 251; Mal. Com. II, p. 172

मुपात्तत्वात् प्रकृतसङ्गतत्वाच्च स आदृतः।मतद्वयमपीदमप्रतिषिद्धत्वात्कौटल्यस्यापीष्टं द्रष्टव्यम् ।

**(2)** Adhikaraṇa VIII, p. 26

 ‘अशक्यं वारयितुम्’इत्यस्य स्थाने ‘अशक्यप्रकृतिश्च’इति नयचन्द्रिकायाः पाठः अप्रतिसमाधेयराजप्रकृतिरूपं च स्वचक्रं भवतीति बोद्धव्यः।

**(3)** Adhikaraṇa IX, p. 61

 ‘नावा यायाद्’ इत्येतदनन्तरं ‘अहिभयाद्’इत्यधिकः पाठो नयचन्द्रिकायाअभिमत इति प्रतीयते ।

**(4)** Adhikaraṇa IX, p. 87

 ‘सार्थव्रजाटवीर्वेति’माधवपाठः।

**(5)** Adhikaraṇa IX, p. 38

 ‘वितंसः पक्षिविश्वासार्थपक्षिरूपालेख्ययोगी देहाच्छादनपटः’इतिमाधवः।

**(6)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 104

 इह ‘अध्यक्षा गुप्तिस्थानं च’ इत्यधिकपाठो नयचन्द्रिकायां प्रतिभाति ।

**(7)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 104

 ‘काम्बोजसौराष्ट्रादयः’इति तु व्याचष्टे माधवः।

**(8)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 114

 माधवस्तु ‘विषम’ इति पठित्वा द्वन्द्वैकवद्भावमाह । ‘नाव’इति च पठति ।

**(9)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 125

 ‘प्राकारतुल्यस्थानतया रथानां स्वबलरक्षकत्व’मिति माधवः।

**(10)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 114

 ‘अभिहत’ इत्यपि माधवपाठः।

**(11)** Adhikaraṇa X, p. 139

 ‘पक्षकक्षोरस्येषु तिर्यक् स्थितौद्वौ दण्डौयस्य स वलयाख्य’इति माधवः।

 These references show that the *Śrīmūlam* commentator held the early writer as an authority to be reckoned withseriously. In the very first instance, he shows his readiness toaccept the reading given by Mādhava despite the fact that noneof the manuscripts supports it. On other occasions he cites the

view of Mādhava to show the difference of opinion since hewas using a different reading on the basis of the manuscriptsavailable to him. Some of the citations show that to grasp thecorrect significance Mādhava's commentary became useful as inthe case of the technical term ‘*vitaṁsa*’which is explained by Mādhava as a camouflage to deceive the birds.

 After the XII Adhikaraṇa of the text Ganapati Sastriproceeds on his own depending solely on the experience gainedin explaining the previous portions. In the XIII Adhikaraṇa inexplaining the passage“हस्तिकामं वा प्रलोभयेयुः”he cites *Pratijñāyaugandharāyaṇa* of Bhāsa as illustration, as follows:⁵⁷यथा प्रतिज्ञायौगन्धरायणे वत्सराजं सालङ्कायनादयः प्रद्योतभृत्या स्वस्वाम्यन्तिकमिति भावः।

In explaining the names of the various medicinal plants he hasdepended upon Suśruta.⁵⁸ But when it comes to the *mantra*portion he could give only the apparent meaning, very oftenfailing to express the real connotation. This he has admittedstating that such technical details can be known only by consulting traditional sources.He observes :⁵⁹
अलिते वलिते स्वाहाइत्येतदन्तस्य मन्त्रस्यार्थःस्पष्ट

पायः सम्प्रदायतो निर्णेयः।

 In explaining the word “Poṭṭalika”— obviously meaninga casket, he draws our attention to the word in the Tamil-Malayalam languages, viz “poṭṭaḷam”meaning a packet orcasket.⁶⁰Towards the end of the Pralambhanādhyāya heobserves that one can only explain the passage to one's ability,in the absence of traditional information. Real significancecan be understood only by following traditional accounts.⁶¹

**दन्तटिप्पणिकास्माभिर्भैषज्यस्यैवमल्पशः।  
क्रमस्तु सर्वस्तस्यापि मन्त्रवत् साम्प्रदायिकः॥**

*A valuable work*: The importance of this work could never be

![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696396457Line.jpg)^(57.)*TSS* 85, p. 189

^(58.)*Ibid,* p. 214

^(59.)*Ibid.* p. 231

^(60.)*Ibid,* p. 233

^(61.)*Ibid,* p. 237

under-rated. Dr. Franklin Edgerton was all praise for the editor. He observed: “Dr. Ganapati Sastri’s edition of the *Kauṭalīya Arthaśāstra*, with commentary, is decidedly the bestedition of that all-important work in existence; the printed text is superior, from the critical scholarly statement, to othereditions and the commentary is of primary and very greatimportance for the interpretation of the very difficult text”⁶².Prof. M. Winternitz had the good fortune of meeting thisdoyen among scholars at his desk while he was engaged in thiswork. He recalls the memorable occasion as follows. “It was agreat pleasure to me when early in November 1923, on myvisit to Trivandrum. I could discuss the subject with the greatPandit. I well remember the stately figure of the Brahmin whoreceived me in his beautiful red robe, speaking Sanskrit clearlyand distinctly so that it was not difficult for a Europeanunused to speaking Sanskrit to understand him. He was alsovery enthusiastic about the new Manuscripts of the *KauṭalīyaArthaśāstra* he had found, and he proudly pointed out to memany improvements of his text on the *editio princeps*, andshowed me the proofs of his own great commentary. The latterwas printed in Nos. 79, 80 and 82, and forms one of the gemsof the whole series. He had found not only new manuscripts ofthe text, but also considerable fragments of the ancientcommentaries of Bhaṭṭasvāmin and Mādhavayajvan. But asthese fragments proved insufficient for an edition of thecommentaries, Ganapati Sastri set to work to write a commentary of his own, making use of the ancient commentaries as faras they were available. Everybody is now convinced of the greatimportance, if not of the great age of the *Arthaśāstra* both forthe social history of the ancient India, and for the history ofIndian Literature. But anybody who has had occasion to studythe *Kauṭalīya*, knows that the work is full of difficulties, withwhich translators and interpreters of the work have hithertostruggled in vain. Hence Ganapati's *Śrīmūla*, as he called his

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(62.)A Souvenir of the Silver Jubilee Celebrations of the Dept. of Publication of Oriental manuscripts, Trivandrum 1934,P. 35

commentary, is an indispensable help for every student of*Arthaśāstra* :⁶³

***CONTROVERSY BETWEEN SHAMA SASTRI****AND GANAPATI SASTRI***

 Ganapati Sastri in his introduction to the first volume ofhis edition made the following observation about the firstedition of *Arthaśāstra* (1909) by Shama Sastri : “I read throughit with an amount of concentration which the rareness andmerit of the work would demand. I found it abounded witherrors, such as the word of a previous sentence joined to asubsequent sentence and vice-versa”It is further noted that theedition contains numerous errors which prompted him to bringout a new edition based on sufficient manuscript materials.

*Press copy*: By sheer chance the present writer was able toprocure the press copy of the textual portion of GanapatiSastri’s edition. What the Trivandrum editor did was toincorporate his textual readings into a printed copy of the1909 Mysore edition. The same was sent to the press alongwith his commentary. Hence now it is possible to pin-pointthe corrections carried out by Ganapati Sastri on the basis offresh manuscripts. Changes effected in the first page of theMysore edition and found printed in the Trivandrum editionmay be noted as follows:



|                             |                          |
|:---------------------------:|:------------------------:|
| ***Mysore edition* **   | ***Trivandrum edition*** |
|      अवरुद्धे वृत्तिः       |    अवरुद्धे च वृत्तिः    |
|        प्रथमाधिकरणम्        |      प्रथममधिकरणम्       |
|         दुर्गनिवेशः         |      दुर्गविनिवेशः       |
|     सन्निधातृचेयकर्म |      |   सन्निधातृनिचयकर्म |    |



Such corrections can be noticed in all the pages of the copywhich substantially represents Ganapati Sastri’s text.

*Objections*: Regarding the statement that “the word of a previous sentence joined to subsequent sentence and vice-versa”, no indication is given by him in the printed text. We have toascertain it from the corrections made by him. A few instancesmay be noted here :

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(63.)Ibid, p. 44

[TABLE]



Thus based on the evidence of manuscripts Ganapati Sastri wasable to reinstate the sentences correctly very often insertingparticles and prepositions missing in the Mysore edition.Shama Sastri is not happy over such corrections and heobserves

:⁶⁴ “There is hardly any change in the meaning due totaking up a word or two with the previous or subsequentsentence. The following are a few instances of his re-arrengement:-

P. 31, lines 9-10 and 16-17; P.40, lines 7-8;  
P.46, lines 5-6; P. 52 lines 8-9; P. 55, lines  
2-3; P. 94, lines 9-10; P. 116, lines 21 and  
P. 117, line 1.

How hollow is the excuse of erroneous readings urged by him for his undertaking what he presumes to be correct edition!”

 This assertion is not correct. Among the eight instancesreferred to by Shama Sastri, the last two may be examined here.

[TABLE]

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**^(64.) Mysore edition, 1924, p. xxxi.

In both the instances the sentence is wrongly split up by theMysore editor and that affects the meaning also. This isgenerally the case with all the instances cited by him. TheTrivandrum editor could print the correct text since he had thebenefit of consulting the ancient Malayalam commentary where the text is correctly quoted and explained. The fact that N.S.Vankatanathacharya, who brought out the fourth revisededition from Mysore had accepted the Trivandrum text in theabove instances indicates the sound position of the Trivandrumeditor.

 A serious and apparently justifiable objection raised byShama Sastri is as follows.⁶⁵“On page 145 line 3 he has splitinto two sentences what in the Mysore edition is taken to be asingle sentence. Taking “पादः पञ्चघटीनाम्” as a separate sentencehe explains it saying that kindling of fire during the five*ghaṭikas* from 12½ to 17½ *ghaṭikas* of the day shall be punishedwith a fine of one-fourth of a *paṇa*. The use of *ghaṭi*in thesense of *ghaṭikā*. 24 minutes, is found nowhere else in the*Arthaśāstra*. The word *ghaṭikāsthāna* in Book II ch. 21 can beexplained otherwise, as done by Bhaṭṭasvāmi by taking it tomean a room in the toll house. As a fine of one-eighth of a*paṇa* is levied for kindling fire during the midday in the previoussentence, this additional fine is not merely superflous but alsocontradictory. It follows therefore that the Mahāmahopādhyāya’s interpretation here is quite wrong and that his splitting the sentence into two is indefensible”.

 This needs a careful examination. Ganapati Sastri hasdeliberately split up the sentence and explained“पञ्चघटीनाम्”to mean a measure of time against the natural meaning of ‘fivepots’as given by Shama Sastri in his translation. The word*ghaṭikāsthāna* also is explained by the Trivandrum editor withan implication to the time factor. He explains it to mean“घटिकात्रयकालावस्थानं”. Now the question is why did he assumesuch a view. He knew that the Malayalam commentary alsomaintains the text as printed from Mysore and explains

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

**^(65.)**Mysore Edition, 1924

पञ्चघटो as five pots. Naturally one has to assume that he hadsome specific reason in changing the Mysore text and to treatthe portion as a separate sentence. In fact, in this respect hewas only following the *Pratipadapañcikā*commentary ofBhaṭṭasvāmi who states : तत्रापि मध्यमासु मध्यमासु पञ्चघटिकासु पादो दण्डः ।Hence Ganapati Sastri could not be accused to havegiven a meaning of his own. He was only accepting the views ofa traditional commentator of *Arthaśāstra*. The Malayalam
commentary which he was using all along explained the portiongiving the meaning ‘five pots’—a view shared by the *Cāṇakyaṭīkā* of Bhikṣuprabhamati who observes: प्रतिगृहम् उदकपूर्णानांपञ्चघटीनाम् प्रकरणे पणपादो दण्डः।

Regarding the mistake in translating *maryādā* as “invariablybe respected”Shama Sastri admits the point though not in somany words. Ganapati Sastri has rightly pointed out that it should be translated as “barrier”. The answer of the Mysoreeditor is that hiswas a free translation or rather paraphrase.

***POINTS OF DEBATE:***

 Then comes the most important aspect of Shama Sastri’scriticism. He has scrupulously collected as many as thirteeninstances where according to him Ganapati Sastri has wronglyexplained the words or passages in the text. He is specific in hisaccusations and hence his remarks need careful attention andscrutiny. “Turning to his commentary, one is obliged to saythat his commentary is as wrong as his recasting of sentenceswhere he departed from the English rendering of the work.”The accusations of the Mysore editor and the apparent reasonswhich Ganapati Sastri might have had for his explanation maybe given as follows:⁶⁶

 **(I)** “On page 16, line 14, he takes the word असत्प्रग्रहto mean अपूज्यपूजन । Neither does असत् mean अपूज्य or प्रग्रह,पूजन ।”

 This meaning is given by Ganapati Sastri on the basisof the following explanation of the Malayalam commen-

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(66.)The page number in this section refers to the pages of the first Mysore edition, 1909.

tator.⁶⁷“Senāpatiyinai asattāyullon oruttannu pūja ceyvānāykoṇteki avan atu ceyyātolincappoḷavane arthamānaṇkaḷeolippatum ceytu kaḷavitu”. This is literally translated intoSanskrit by the *Śrīmūlam* commentator as :⁶⁸असत्प्रग्रहेण अवक्षिप्तः अपूज्यपूजनेन निमित्तेन परिभूतः। अपूज्यपूजने राज्ञा चोदितस्तदकुर्वन्नर्थपानाभ्यां हापित इत्यर्थः

 The position of the Trivandrum editor is well taken andis based on traditional views.

 **(2)** “On page 35, line 8 his explanation of the wordकुल as बहुपुत्रसंघ is wrong”.

 This explanation is really based on the Malayalampassage:⁶⁹ “antiye rājaputranmārellākkum rājyam pakuttukoṭuppitu”— meaning that the country shall be divided amongall the sons of the king. Here again the Sanskritexplanation isauthoritative.

 **(3)** “On page 37, line 2, he takes प्रयासयेत्, in the sense of हन्यात्,should kill, without quoting any authority for it”.

 Here again the authority of Ganapati Sastri is the Malayalam commentary.⁷⁰The Sanskrit explanation is अधार्मिकं पुत्रं हन्यादित्यर्थःis only the translation of “adhārmikanāyiruntaavaruddhane kolvitu”. Ganapati Sastri should have mentionedthis authority since the explanation is rather technical anddifferent from the natural connotation of the word, one maysay.

 **(4) “**On page 47. line 6 परिहारः दोस्थ्यपरिहारेण स्वास्थ्यसिद्ध्यर्थंदीयमानं द्रव्यम् ।

 This is quite wrong. Compare : पञ्चवार्षिकः परिहारःetc; onP. 170 lines 2-5”

 The meaning of परिहार as remission of tax in the secondinstance is correct and is accepted by Ganapati Sastri also. It is

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(67.)*Kauṭalīya* with Malayalam commentary, 1,p. 93

^(68.)*TSS* 79, p. 49

^(69.)*Kauṭalīya* with Malayalam commentary, I, p. 138

^(70.)Ibid, I, p. 142

in the first instance that the learned scholars differ. The meanings offered by the Trivandrum editor is that the king should provide financial assistance to save the inhabitants from natural calamities so that it will indirectly help to maintain his own financial position. This meaning is not far from the connotation of the word and is in agreement with the idea of the Malayalam commentator also.

 **(5)** “On page 57, line 5बाहिरिकान् कितववञ्चकनटनर्तकान्। Authority is not quoted”.

 The authority of Ganapati Sastri is the following remarks of the Malayalam commentator:⁷¹“Bāhirikar āvor kitavavañcaka-yācaka-naṭa-nartakādikal”. In fact, the *Śrīmulam* commentator has left out the word ‘yācaka’from the list of his authority. The word is explained in the same way on another occasion also by the Malayalam authority as well as his Sanskrit translator. In explaining the portion : द्वारबाहिरिकादियं च दुर्गम्। the Malayalam commentator explains the wordas:⁷²“Dvārabāhirikādeyam enta vāru vātal kākkum avanu auṭukkutum naṭa-nartakādikaliṭe koḷḷumatum”Ganapati Sastri translates the portion in his commentary as:⁷³द्वारबाहिरिकसम्बन्धि आदेयं पुरादिद्वारपालंर्भूतित्वेन ग्राह्यं बहिरिकेभ्यो नटनर्तकादिभ्यो राज्ञा ग्राह्यञ्चेति यावत् ।

** (6) “**On page 60, line 1, लक्षणाध्यक्षः क्षेत्रारामादिसीमाचिह्वाध्यक्षः। This is wrong. Compare p. 84, line 3.”

 In the second instance the word undisputedly means mintmaster. There is no difference of opinion. But in the case of the first, Shama Sastri objects to the above explanation which is really based on the Malayalam commentary as follows:⁷⁴“Lakṣaṇādhyakṣan tāpaṭipakkumavanum”. Here the malaya-

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(71.)*Kauṭalīyam* with Malayalam commentary, II, p. 34

^(72.)*Ibid,* p. 40

^(73.)*TSS* 79, p. 136

^(74.)*Kauṭalīyam* Malayalam commentary II, p. 40

lam commentator states that the officer is in charge of surveying the place. The words: क्षेत्रारामादिis of course Ganapati Sastri’s own explanation. It is not clear whether he has any authority for that.

 **(7)** “On page 60, line 14: व्याजी विंशतिभागः। This restriction to twentieth part is wrong. It means 5 percent or 7 percent commissions also.”

 Ganapati Sastri’s explanation is : व्याजी विशतिभागःपुनर्माने माभूदूनतेत्यधिकं गृह्यमाणः। This is only the translation of the Malayalam commentary: “Vyājiyāvatu nūttil añcu koḷḷumatu; nāli vāciyum”. In measuring grains it is usual to add a handful after the required quantity is measured. This is to compensate for the loss if any. The same meaning is given by the Malayalam commentator on other occasions also: Here is aninstance:⁷⁵ “Vyāji iraṇṭu jāti, nuttāl añcu kollumatu nāḷi vāśiyum”. The idea of the seven percent suggested by Shama Sastri is not at all mentioned in this early commentary of anonymous Kerala author.

 **(8)** “On Page 60, line 14: परिक्षः आतरद्रव्यं meaning ferry due. Again on page 85, line 2, the same word is taken by him to mean पारीक्षिकम्thus contradicting himself.”

 It is true that Ganapati Sastri gives the meaning as आतरद्रव्यम् by translating the passage of the Malayalam commentator:⁷⁷“Parigham āvitu toṇikaṭattikoḷḷumatu”. The second meaning again is based on the same ancient commentary:⁷⁸“Parigham āvitu parīkṣikkintavan Koḷḷum atu”. In both the instances the general connection is the same, namely ‘the fee or remuneration for a particular work’and hencs there is no contradiction in the statement of the ancient commentator or on the part of his Sanskrit translator.

** (9)** “On page 60, line 30, राजवर्षं मासः पक्षो दिवसश्च ब्युष्टम् —राजवर्षादचतुष्टयं व्युष्टसंज्ञमित्यर्थः इति व्याख्यानम् ।नेयं संज्ञा सोक-

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(75.)*Kauṭalīyam*, Malayalam commentary, II p. 42

^(76.**)*Ibid,* p. 124

^(77.)*Ibid*, p. 42

प्रसिद्धा प्रयोगाभावात्, परं तु ग्रन्थकृतस्स्वसंज्ञा शास्त्रे व्यवहारार्थं कृता इति वक्तव्यम् ।

Further, authority is not quoted. If however *vyuṣṭa* is taken to mean the four things, royal year. month, fortnight and day, then the use of the word, काल along with व्युष्ट on page 64, lines 16, 17 and 19 will be meaningless”.

 In the particular instance Ganapati Sastri has explained *Vyuṣṭa* to mean the regnal year, month, fortnight and the day and has illustrated in general terms in the following lines:⁷⁹एतच्च अमुकराजवर्षेऽमुकमासेऽमक पक्षेऽमुकपुरुषेणानीतमेतावद् धनम् अद्यामुकपुरुषायैतावद् दत्तमिति रीत्या निबन्धपुस्तकादिषु लेख्यमिति बोद्धव्यम् ।

For the word काल in the other instances mentioned above, he gives the meaning वर्षादिः—the rainy season etc. In giving these connotations he has scrupulously followed the traditional view of the ancient Malayalam commentator, hence it cannot be said that his statements are without any authority. The Malayalam commentary is as follows:⁸⁰“Rājavarṣam māsam pakṣam divasam innālinnum vyuṣṭam enpitu samjña. Rājavarṣam āvitu rājā vāḷveriya saṁvatsaram tuṭaṅkiyuḷḷa saṁvatsarankal. Atinuḷḷa masamum ammāsattilulla pakṣamum pakṣattiluḷḷa divasamum elutumārāvitu. Rājāvu. mahāsenanukku cellān'nta ayyāṇtemāntiṅkalmuapakkattu pañcami nālinnon koṇtuvanna dhanam innittanai innonnu innittanai koṭukkitentu ijjāti”.

 The Malayalam commentator has given the illustration as “in the fifth regnal year of king Mahāsena, in the particular month of *Hemanta*, in the first fortnight and on the fifth day, so and so has brought so much amount”etc. He further states that the regnal year may be divided into three parts, each consisting of four months. The first of the three is called *Varṣā*

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

***^(78.)****Kauṭalīyam, with Malayalam Commentary II p. 124*

*^(79.)ITSS, 79, p. 138*

*^(80.) Kauṭalīyam Malayalam commentary, II, p. 44*

the other two being *Hemanta* and *Grīṣma*. Of the three, the first called *Varṣā* is being referred to as *kāla* in the above instances pointed out by the Mysore editor.

** (10)** “On page 60 line 21, बर्षाहेमन्तग्रीष्माणां तृतीयसप्तमा दिवसोनाः पक्षाः शेषाः पूर्णाः इति राजवर्षस्य त्रिधा विभक्तस्य सिंहकन्यातुलावृश्चिकाश्चत्वारो रविमासा बर्षर्तुरित्येको भागः... इति व्याख्यातम् ।

 इयं व्याख्या चारणक्यकालिकज्योतिषसिद्धान्तग्रन्थकत्रंभिप्रायोभयाज्ञानविजृम्भितमेव ।

Here Mr. T. Ganapati Sastri takes the year to be a solar year of 365^(1/₄)days made up of twelve Saṅkramaṇa months divided into three seasons, and in the 24 fortnights of this year 6 days are in his opinion to be omitted. This results in a year of 359 days. What year is this? Nothing can be more absurd than this”.

 Here again, *Śrīmulam* commentator has devotedly followed the traditional view expressed by the ancient Malayalam commentator and hence he cannot be found fault with for propounding a theory of his own without any basis. The Malayalam commentator has grouped the regnal year into three seasons, mentioning by name the different months included in it. There will be four months in each group. Similarly, there will be 8 pakṣas or fortnights in each of the three seasons. Among the fortnights, the third and seventh will be lesser in duration by one day each. Thus in a year there will be a shortage of six days. This classification is for the purpose of keeping the accounts. This need not be the exact astronomical truth, it seems. This is what has been suggested by him in the following passage:⁸¹

“Immūntu kūttilum oro kūttil nālu tiṅkaḷilum eṭṭeṭṭu pakṣam ulavām. Avattil mūntām pakṣattilum olām pakṣattilum oro gāl kuraivitu entiprakāram muntu kuttilum āru nāl curuṅkuvitu...entu vyavahārthamāyulla kālam mutifcitu”.

 Here the real position is that Shama Sastri went by the natural import of the words whereas Ganapati Sastri depended

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(81.)Kautaliayam with Malayalam Commentary, p. 44

on a traditional view which is the only proper approach in explaining an age-old scientific treatise of this kind.

** (11)** “On page 64, lines 15, 16, 17 व्युष्टादिविवरणयुक्ताम् आयगणनां सम्पादयेदित्यर्थः इति विवररणं केवलं शब्दाडम्बर एव ।

This means that he should secure the accounts of receipts containing the explanations of *Vyuṣṭa* and other words. Can there be anything more nonsensical than this?”

 The observation is the result of misunderstanding the real import of the passage. Here again the explanation is based on the Malayalam commentary which correctly explains the significance. It does not mean that the receipts of accounts should contain the connotations of *Vyuṣṭa* and other terms. What it really means is that the receipts should mention the regnal year, the month, the place, the actual amount, obtained from whom etc. In other words the account maintained should be detailed so that it can be verified at a later date to the minute details. It does not mean that the accountant is responsible to explain the lexical meaning of words. While Ganapati Sastri has put it briefly, the Malayalam commentator has made it more explicit as follows.⁸² “Kīlakkaliñña kālam inna tiñkal inna deśattu ittanai dhanam innoṅkan munne rājāvinu entiṅñane ollatn vyuṣṭadeśakālam āvitu.

  It means that the income due to the king was remitted by so and so on such a date before the particular authority. The English translation of Shama Sastri that “the expenditure shall on the *Vyuṣṭa* or new year's day, be verified” ⁸³etc; is really off the mark.

 **(12)** “On page 65 line 15” युक्तप्रतिषेधः युक्तानामध्यक्षाणां घनापहाराद्वारणम् । कि घनापहारः अध्यक्षैःराजसमक्षमेव क्रियते येन राजातांस्तस्माद् वारयेत् अत इदं व्याख्यानमसङ्गतमेव ।”

 Here Ganapati Sastri has given a detailed explanation:⁸⁴

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(82.)Kautaliyam, with Malayalam Commentary, p. 57

^(83.)Mysore, 1923, p. 70

^(84.)TSS 79, p. 152

युक्तानामव्यक्षाणां प्रतिषेधो घनापहाराद्वारणम् उत्कोचग्रहणनिमित्ताद्वा प्रजापोडनाद् वा वारणम् ।

For this he has his basis on the Malayalam commentary which actually states something more.⁸⁵ “Yuktapratiṣedham āvitu adhyakṣaril nintum rājaputraril nintum prajaikkuvarum pīḍaiolippitu”. It means that the term stands for the prevention by authorities and the sons of kings, If the people of this category extract wealth, without good intentions, it will naturally affect the income of the state. Their act will be of the nature of misappropriation of funds due to the king. This is sought to be explained by the Trivandrum commentator and it cannot be termed as far-fetched.

** (13)** “P. 67, line 8 ः उपयुक्तः युक्तानामुपरि नियुक्तः, one who is appointed above Yuktas. This is contradictory to the meaning of the same word given by him on page 52, line 4. There he saysः युक्तः प्रधानः उपयुक्तः तत्सहकारी ।”

 Here the position taken by the Mysore editor is apparently justifiable. Ganapati Sastri has explained the word उपयुक्तin the sense of a superior officer in the first instance and as a colleague, apparently junior, on the second occasion. This needs an explanation. The contradiction is owing to his dependence on the Malayalam commentator who explains the instances as follows :⁸⁶

 **(i)** “Upayuktan āvon adhyakṣarakku menokki ceyyumavan”.

**(ii)** “Upayuktan āvon aupakārikan”.

The meaning of the first that he is a supervising officer is expressed by the terms :युक्तानामुपरि नियुक्तः । The Malayalam term ओपकारिका meaning one who gives his service is translated as तत्सहकारीby the *Śrīmūlam* commentator. One has to concede that he was depending on a traditional explanation. He could have saved himself from the embarrassment of the contradic-

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(85.)Kauṭalīya with Malayalam commentary, II, p. 60

^(86.)*Ibid,* pp. 67, 38

tion by mentioning his authority as भाषाटीकाas he did in instances like TSS I. p. 140, 141 and 225.

***EDITORIAL DRAWBACKS:***

 Shama Sastri has been severe in his criticism of his counter part. He is of the opinion that the Trivandrum edition is not at all a worthy attempt. He observes: “Another serious defect of his edition is the omission of all various readings”

 This indeed is a serious charge levelled against the well known editor of the famous Trivandrum Sanskrit series in which he had already published 78 works on a variety of subjects. The present work is the 79th editorial effort of the great Pandit. In a text book of this character the possibility of coming across meaningful readings other than scribal errors is rather limited. Further, the fidelity of the manuscripts has been brought out by the following observations of the learned editor in his introduction. “They are complete and written in Malayalam characters and almost free from errors." As the Mysore editor has imagined the number of readings will not be large.

***EDITOR'S PERSPECTIVE:***

 Ganapati Sastri concerned himself only with meaningful readings as can be gathered from his statement in the उपोद्घात to the third part of the work :

व्यावृत्तानामर्थंवतामस्मत्पुस्तकस्थानां पाठविशेषाणां सूचनिका काचिदिह प्रथमपरिशिष्टात्मा निवेशिता ।

 As is evident from the first part, the editor has made use of four manuscripts designated by him as क, ख, ग,and घः In this part he has given as footnotes nearly forty readings collected from his critical apparatus. See for instance, pages 2, 14, 52, 54, 63, 6S, 65, 67, 69, 80, 81, 84, 85, 86, 91, 104 etc. This practice was discontinued in the subsequent volumes for some unknown reason. All along he was promising to give a comparative table as appendix and this he provided in 79 pages of the third volume. In addition to this he has discussed the important variants in the course of his commentary. “Such of the variants that have special import to convey are dealt with in the commentary. Improvements of this nature will be

obvious from a perusal of the text and the commentary”observes Ganapati Sastri.

 As already stated he secured a copy of the Mysore edition (1909) and noted down his readings in its pages correcting the mistakes here and there. In fact he substantially changed the printed text to transform it as his press copy. He started with the intention of giving all the different variants in the footnote as he was wont to do in his previous editorial projects. The Mysore readings rejected by him on the basis of manuscript evidence were noted down in his press copy as मुद्रितपुस्तकपाठः ।But on second thought he scored them off retaining only the variants from his own manuscripts. He felt that the Mysore readings were so profuse and teeming with errors so as to demand a separate treatment in the appendix and he did it also. After noting the variants in the first 20 pages of the printed version he decided to eschew the practice and to be selective. This is what really happened. The present writer is of the opinion that Ganapati Sastri omitted the readings of the different manuscripts in the later parts of the text for the sake of convenience. Still, one has to admit that it has deprived the text of what would have been an excellent and valuable addition enhancing the worth of the treatise.

 The Mysore text was changed drastically by inserting numbers, deleting full stop where it was not suited to the text of the Trivandrum editor, providing full stops where it was found necessary, changing full stops to semi-colon, re-arrenging paragraphs, re-casting chapter titles and colophons by changing the sequence of words, taking away or adding quotation marks, scoring off foot notes and correcting the numerous printers devils. All this he was able to do since he wisely chose a printed text to prepare his press copy.

***THE TONE OF DIALOGUE :***

 Before concluding this section the present writer feels it necessary to say something about the tone of the dialogue or rather controversy between two of the greatest scholars that the early part of the 19th century has produced. Ganapati Sastri has unwittingly invited the wrath of his counterpart by stating that the Mysore edition “abounded with

errors”. B it he also admitted that the nature of the text was such that “even a talented Pandit cannot hope to easily understand it”and for that “sufficient manuscripts material was indispensible”. Regarding the English translation the Trivandrum editor cited just one instance and said :” I do not see how this meaning was made out". He further felt that the purification of the text alone will not suffice, that the meaning has also to be preserved from misinterpretations”. This is all what Ganapati Sastri said about the Mysore editor.

 These remarks, apparently made in good taste and with a critical spirit provoked Shama Sastri to the core to unleash a spate of criticism, often based on grounds not so sure since he was not in a position to verify them. His Sanskrit introduction to the third edition issued in the year 1924 contains the following uncharitable observations

 **(1)**तृतीयमुद्रणमिदमर्थशास्त्रस्य न द्वितीयमुद्ररणादतीव भिद्यत इति नोपोद्धातान्तरमपेक्षते । तथापि महामहोपाध्यायेन गणपतिशास्त्रिरणा स्वीयव्याख्यया साकमनन्तशयनसंस्कृतग्रन्थावल्यां प्रकाशितस्यार्थशास्त्रप्रथमाधिकरणद्वयम्योपोद्घाते महीशूरराजकीयसंस्कृतग्रन्थावल्यां प्रकाशितमर्थशास्त्रमूलं पाठायुविभूयिष्ठं तदीयाङ्गलेयभाषानुवादश्चासङ्गतार्थं इति यत् प्रलपितं यच्च स्वप्रकाशितं मलं व्याख्यानं च वाढं शुद्धं सङ्गत चेति प्रोद्घुष्टं तदत्र किञ्चिद् विचार्यते ।

  अनूयान्धीकृतदशाऽनेन शास्त्रिरणा दृष्टापाठाशुद्धिः पूर्ववाक्ययोज्यस्योत्तरवाक्येन सह योजनमनरवाक्प्रयोज्यस्य पूर्ववाक्येन सह योजनमित्येवंजातीयेत्यबर्णि।

** (2)**कि

ञ्चान व्याख्याने गणपतिशास्त्रिरणा “अग्निकार्य” शब्दोऽनेकवारं प्रमुक्तो दृश्यते। अग्निकार्यशब्दोऽ- ग्न्युपासनमभिधत्ते न तु लौकिकमग्न्युद्दीपनमिति नाद्यापि तेन ज्ञातमिति विस्मयावहमेतत् ।

** (3)** अपि चमर्यादाशव्दस्य तात्पर्यायं पुरस्कारमुपादाय कृतमाङ्गलेयभाषानुवादमधिक्षिपन् गणपतिशास्त्री स्वीये पदप्रयोगे पदशक्यार्थमपि न बर्णयतीति विस्मयावहमेतत् ।

** (4)** तदेवं सत्यामपि स

म्यास्यत्रयमातकासामग्र्यामेतैरन्यैश्च बहुभिर्दोषैःपरिपूर्णा गणपतिशास्त्रिणःकृतिरित्येतद् विस्मयावहम्।

 In his English introduction to the same volume also there are a few more observations of a similar nature, if not more vehement in tone.

 **(1)** “It follows therefore that the Mahāmahopādhyāya’s interpretation here is quite wrong and that his splitting the sentence into two is indefensible. Another serious objection to this interpretation is the violation of Grammar”.

 **(2)** “Even an ordinary student of Sanskrit knows that 'pāda' never means a 'daṇḍa', but only a quarter”.

 Shama Sastri concludes his tirade with a challenging note as follows: “Whether in the face of these and other errors to point out here, it is fair for the Mahāmahopādhyāya to find fault with the Mysore edition of the text and its English version, is a question that is left to scholars for decision”.

***GANAPATI SASTRI VINDICATED :***

*** ***But it is gratifying to note that N S Venkatanathacharya who brought out the revised fourth edition of the Mysore text in 1960 after the sad demise of his illustrious predecessor Shama Sastri (who passed away on 23rd January, 1944) has made amends and kept the great tradition of true and  
unbiased scholarship. Without the least hesitation he acceptedthe good readings and explanations of Ganapati Sastri which he felt was necessary to make his edition upto-date and free from errors of omission and commission. This he has admitted in his introductory statement as follows:⁸⁷

 तत्रापि श्रीमद्भिः टि गणपतिनाश्त्रिभिः अङ्गीकृतः पाठः पदार्थो वा यत्र समीचीनतया भातः तत्र स एवाङ्गीकृत इति च ।

It is true that in doing this he has obliterated the text of Shama Sastri and made the English translation incompatible with the present text. But that is a different problem. What assumes significance is that the latest editor from Mysore was able to see through the working of the mind of his predecessors In a footnote to the introduction of Shama Sastri which he reproduced in his edition, he observes:⁸⁸

**![](../../../books_images/U-IMG-1696316066Line.jpg)**

^(87.)Mysore, 1960, p. xi

^(88.)Ibid, p. XXXV

किञ्चश्रीशामाशास्त्रिणां श्रीगणपतिशास्त्रिरर्णां च कारणान्तरप्राप्तात्कालिकमनोवृत्तिभेदेन परस्परमुद्भाविता आरोपिताश्च एतादृशाः दोषाःकिञ्चिद्समाहितमनःपरिणामा इति, नैषां दोषाणां तावद्याथार्थ्यं सम्भवेदिति च समाहितैः विभावनीयम् ।

 It is true that extra-academic considerations too have gone into in the course of this controversy. But that does not diminish the contribution made by the two great savants to the study of Kauṭalya's *Arthaśāstra.*

***EDITIONS AND TRANSLATIONS***  
 Editions and translations of this important text have appeared from different institutions in India and abroad. For a detailed bibliographical account see: *“Bibliography of Kauṭiliya Arthaśāstra.*” by Ludwik Sternbach, Vishwesharanand Research Institute, Hoshiarpur, Punjab, 1973, pp. 39. Since studies embracing the different aspects of the work are being published from different places from time to time no such account can claim to be complete. Some of the important editions and translations may alone be noted here.
